<UML:Description reserve="295" >A boundary is a class that lies on the periphery of a system, but within it.  It interacts with actors outside the system as well as with entity, control, and other boundary classes within the system.

<UML:Stereotype id="d2XwdVKGK0CIb+BHClF46g" >
<UML:Description reserve="715" >(Name for the stereotyped class is Realization.) Specifies a realization relationship between a specification model element or elements (the supplier) and a model element or elements that implement it (the client). The implementation model element is required to support all of the operations or received signals that the specification model element declares. The implementation model element must make or inherit its own declarations of the operations and signal receptions. The mapping specifies the relationship between the two. The mapping may or may not be computable. Realization can be used to model stepwise refinement, optimizations, transformations, templates, model synthesis, framework composition, etc.</UML:Description>

<UML:Stereotype id="OIq1ILNC/0yPeRaifF+PpA" >
<UML:Description reserve="363" >A metamodel is a stereotyped model denoting that the model is an abstraction of another model, i.e., it is a model of a model. Hence, if M2 is a model of the model M1, then M2 is a metamodel of M1. It follows then that classes in M1 are instances of metaclasses in M2. The stereotype can be recursively applied, as in the case of a 4-layer metamodel architecture.</UML:Description>

<UML:Stereotype id="bGFyd6DOqEW5CMbHcFSCEQ" >
<UML:Description reserve="715" >(Name for the stereotyped class is Realization.) Specifies a realization relationship between a specification model element or elements (the supplier) and a model element or elements that implement it (the client). The implementation model element is required to support all of the operations or received signals that the specification model element declares. The implementation model element must make or inherit its own declarations of the operations and signal receptions. The mapping specifies the relationship between the two. The mapping may or may not be computable. Realization can be used to model stepwise refinement, optimizations, transformations, templates, model synthesis, framework composition, etc.</UML:Description>
<UML:DescriptionResourceID>94</UML:DescriptionResourceID>
<UML:ElementKind>Abstraction</UML:ElementKind>
<UML:Name>realize</UML:Name>
<UML:NameResourceID>34</UML:NameResourceID>
</UML:Stereotype>
<UML:Stereotype id="kGfEdiiMEEGAoCcKxA+6qQ" >
<UML:Description reserve="433" >(Name for the stereotyped class is Refinement.) Specifies refinement relationship between model elements at different semantic levels, such as analysis and design. The mapping specifies the relationship between the two elements or sets of elements. The mapping may or may not be computable, and it may be unidirectional or bidirectional. Refinement can be used to model transformations from analysis to design and other such changes.</UML:Description>

<UML:Stereotype id="hOJwkLteE0m/xiyM5RUezQ" >
<UML:Description reserve="469" >(Name for the stereotyped class is Trace.) Specifies a trace relationship between model elements or sets of model elements that represent the same concept in different models. Traces are mainly used for tracking requirements and changes across models. Since model changes can occur in both directions, the directionality of the dependency can often be ignored. The mapping specifies the relationship between the two, but it is rarely computable and is usually informal.</UML:Description>
